ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-item {
    counter-increment: list-counter-alpha;
}

ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-marker::before {
    content: counter(list-counter-alpha, lower-alpha);
}

/* Level 3: Lowercase roman numerals */

    counter-reset: list-counter-roman;
}

    counter-increment: list-counter-roman;
}

ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-marker::before {
    content: counter(list-counter-roman, lower-roman);
}

<p>COLLINS &amp; BOSCO [KMTC NRB CAMPUS. MAR &amp; SEPT 2020] NEUROLOGICAL NURSING</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="neurological-nursing">NEUROLOGICAL NURSING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#neurological-nursing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="review-of-a-p-of-ns">REVIEW OF A &amp; P OF NS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#review-of-a-p-of-ns" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>The nervous system consists of two divisions: the central nervous system (CNS), including the brain and spinal cord, and the peripheral nervous system, made up of the cranial and spinal nerves.</li>
<li>The peripheral nervous system can be further divided into the</li>
<li>somatic, or voluntary, nervous system, and</li>
<li>the autonomic, or involuntary, nervous system.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="peripheral-nervous-system">PERIPHERAL NERVOUS SYSTEM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#peripheral-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The Somatic Nervous/voluntary System consists of nerves that:</p>
<ul>
<li>Convey sensory information to the CNS.</li>
<li>Transmit messages for motor movement from the CNS to the body.</li>
<li>31 spinal nerves</li>
<li>12 cranial nerves</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="autonomic-involuntary-nervous-system">Autonomic/ involuntary nervous system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#autonomic-involuntary-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>The autonomic nervous system regulates the automatic behaviors of the body (heart rate, blood pressure, respiration, digestion etc).</li>
<li>The autonomic nervous system can be divided into two subsystems:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>The Sympathetic Nervous System</li>
<li>The Parasympathetic Nervous System</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="sympathetic-nervous-system">Sympathetic nervous system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sympathetic-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Is a network of nerves that prepares the organs for rigorous activity:</p>
<ul>
<li>increases heart rate, blood pressure, respiration, etc. ("fight or flight" response)</li>
<li>comprised of ganglia on the left and right of the spinal cord</li>
<li>mainly uses norepinephrine as a neurotransmitter at the postganglionic synapses.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="parasympathetic-nervous-system">Parasympathetic nervous system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#parasympathetic-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Facilitates vegetative, nonemergency responses by the organs.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>decreases functions increased by the sympathetic nervous system.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Comprised of long preganglion axons extending from the spinal cord and short postganglionic fibers that attach to the organs themselves.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>dominant during our relaxed states.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Postganglionic axons mostly release acetylcholine as a neurotransmitter</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-2bfe7dbb.jpeg" alt="img-0.jpeg">
 2007 Thomson Higher Education</p>
<p> The function of the nervous system is to control all motor, sensory, autonomic, cognitive, and behavioral activities
 The nervous system has approximately 10 million sensory neurons that send information about the internal and external environment to the brain and 500,000 motor neurons that control the muscles and glands.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="neurones">NEURONES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#neurones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The basic functional unit of the brain is the neuron.</li>
<li>It is composed of a cell body, a dendrite, and an axon.</li>
<li>The dendrite is a branch-type structure with synapses for receiving electrochemical messages</li>
<li>The axon is a long projection that carries impulses away from the cell body.</li>
<li>Nerve cell bodies occurring in clusters are called ganglia or nuclei.</li>
<li>A cluster of cell bodies with the same function is called a center (eg, the respiratory center).</li>
<li>Neuroglial cells, another type of nerve cell, support, protect, and nourish neurons.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="neurotransmitters">Neurotransmitters<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#neurotransmitters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Neurotransmitters communicate messages from one neuron to another or from a neuron to a specific target tissue.</li>
<li>Neurotransmitters are manufactured and stored in synaptic vesicles.</li>
</ul>
<p>COLLINS &amp; BOSCO [KMTC NRB CAMPUS. MAR &amp; SEPT 2020] NEUROLOGICAL NURSING</p>
<ul>
<li>They enable conduction of impulses across the synaptic cleft.</li>
<li>When released, the neurotransmitter crosses the synaptic cleft and binds to receptors in the postsynaptic cell membrane.</li>
<li>The action of a neurotransmitter is to potentiate, terminate, or modulate a specific action and can either excite or inhibit the target cell's activity
Many neurologic disorders are due,
to an imbalance in neurotransmittersthat is, a lack of gamma aminobutyric acid (GABA) and acetylcholine e.g. in Huntington's disease, low serotonin levels in some forms of epilepsy, and a decrease in dopamine in Parkinson's disease.</li>
<li>In fact, probably all brain functions are modulated through neurotransmitter receptor site activity, including memory and other cognitive processes.</li>
<li>They can be excitatory or inhibitory and are rapid-acting (measured in milliseconds).</li>
</ul>
<p> Acetylcholine (major transmitter of the parasympathetic nervous system)
Serotonin
Dopamine
Norepinephrine (major transmitter of the sympathetic nervous system)
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal"></mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm"></span></span></span></span></span>  Gamma-aminobutyric acid (GABA)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anatomy-of-the-brain">ANATOMY OF THE BRAIN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anatomy-of-the-brain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The brain is divided into three major areas:</p>
<p>the cerebrum,
brain stem,
the cerebellum.</p>
<ul>
<li>The cerebrum is composed of two hemispheres, the thalamus, the hypothalamus, and the basal ganglia.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-124a19b1.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<p>Cerebrum. The cerebrum consists of two hemispheres that are incompletely separated by the great longitudinal fissure.</p>
<ul>
<li>This sulcus separates the cerebrum into the right and left hemispheres.</li>
<li>The outside surface of the hemispheres has a wrinkled appearance that is the result of many folded layers or convolutions called gyri, which increase the surface area of the brain, accounting for the high level of activity carried out by such a small-appearing organ</li>
<li>The cerebral hemispheres are divided into four parts: frontal, parietal, temporal, and occipital lobes. The four lobes are as follows:</li>
<li>Frontalthe largest lobe. The major functions of this lobe are concentration, abstract thought, information storage or memory, and motor function. It also contains Broca's area, critical for motor control of speech.</li>
<li>Parietala predominantly sensory lobe. The primary sensory cortex, which analyzes sensory information and relays the interpretation of this information to the thalamus and other cortical areas, is located in the parietal lobe.
Temporalcontains the auditory receptive areas. Contains a vital area called the interpretive area that provides integration of somatization, visual, and auditory areas.
Occipitalthe posterior lobe of the cerebral hemisphere is responsible for visual interpretation.</li>
<li>The corpus callosum is a thick collection of nerve fibers that connects the two hemispheres of the brain and is responsible for the transmission of information from one side of the brain to the other</li>
<li>The basal ganglia are masses of nuclei located deep in the cerebral hemispheres that are responsible for control of fine motor movements, including those of the hands and lower extremities.
The thalamus lies on either side of the third ventricle and acts primarily as a relay station for all sensation except smell. All memory, sensation, and pain impulses also pass through this section of the brain.
The hypothalamus is located anterior and inferior to the thalamus.
The hypothalamus lies immediately beneath and lateral to the lower portion of the wall of the third ventricle.
The hypothalamus plays an important role in the endocrine system because it regulates the pituitary secretion of hormones that influence metabolism,</li>
</ul>
<p>COLLINS &amp; BOSCO [KMTC NRB CAMPUS. MAR &amp; SEPT 2020] NEUROLOGICAL NURSING</p>
<p>reproduction, stress response, and urine production.</p>
<ul>
<li>It works with the pituitary to maintain fluid balance and maintains temperature regulation by promoting vasoconstriction or vasodilation.</li>
<li>The hypothalamus is the site of the hunger center and is involved in appetite control.</li>
<li>The pituitary gland is located in the sella turcica at the base of the brain and is connected to the hypothalamus. The pituitary is a common site for brain tumors in adults.</li>
<li>Brain Stem. The brain stem consists of the midbrain, pons, and medulla oblongata.</li>
<li>The midbrain connects the pons and the cerebellum with the cerebral hemispheres; it contains sensory and motor pathways and serves as the center for auditory and visual reflexes.</li>
<li>Cranial nerves III (Oculomotor) and IV (Trochlear) originate in the midbrain.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cranial-nerves">CRANIAL NERVES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cranial-nerves" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>I. Olfactory
II. Optic
III. Oculomotor
IV. Trochlear
V. Trigeminal
VI. Abducent
VII. Facial
VIII. Vestibulocochlear (auditory)
IX. Glossopharyngeal
X. Vagus
XI. Accessory
XII. Hypoglossal</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mnemonics">MNEMONICS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mnemonics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>CRANIAL NERVES: Oh Oh Oh Tiny Tits Are Fun And Give
Virgins Awkward Hips</p>
<p>FUNCTIONAL TYPES: Some Say Marry Money But My Brother Says Big Brains Matter More (S- Sensory, M- Motor, B-Both Sensory and Motor</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The pons is situated in front of the cerebellum between the midbrain and the medulla and is a bridge between the two halves of the cerebellum, and between the medulla and the cerebrum.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cranial nerves V (Trigeminal) through VIII (Vestibulocochlear (auditory) connect to the brain in the pons.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The pons contains motor and sensory pathways. Portions of the pons also control the heart, respiration, and blood pressure.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The medulla oblongata contains motor fibers from the brain to the spinal cord and sensory fibers from the spinal cord to the brain.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cranial nerves IX (Glossopharyngeal) through XII(Hypoglossal) connect to the brain in the medulla</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cerebellum. The cerebellum is separated from the cerebral hemispheres by a fold of dura mater, the tentorium cerebelli.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The cerebellum has both excitatory and inhibitory actions and is largely responsible for coordination of movement.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It also controls fine movement, balance, position sense (awareness of where each part of the body is), and integration of sensory input.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<table><thead><tr><th>Table 14.1 Cranial Nerves</th><th></th><th></th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>NAME</td><td>NUMBER</td><td>FUNCTION</td><td>ACTIVITY</td></tr><tr><td>Olfactory</td><td>I</td><td>Sensory</td><td>Sense of smell.</td></tr><tr><td>Optic</td><td>II</td><td>Sensory</td><td>Vision.</td></tr><tr><td>Oculomotor</td><td>III</td><td>Motor</td><td>Pupillary reflex, extrinsic muscle movement of eye.</td></tr><tr><td>Trochlear</td><td>IV</td><td>Motor</td><td>Eye-muscle movement.</td></tr><tr><td>Trigeminal</td><td>V</td><td>Mixed</td><td>Ophthalmic branch: Sensory impulses from scalp, upper eyelid, nose, cornea, and lacrimal gland. Motor action includes teeth clenching, movement of mandible.</td></tr><tr><td>Abducens</td><td>VI</td><td>Mixed</td><td>Extrinsic muscle movement of eye.</td></tr><tr><td>Facial</td><td>VII</td><td>Mixed</td><td>Taste (sinterior two thirds of tongue). Facial movements such as smiling, closing of eyes, frowning. Production of tears and salivary stimulation.</td></tr><tr><td>Vestibulocochlear</td><td>VIII</td><td>Sensory</td><td>Vestibular branch: Sense of balance or equilibrium. Cochlear branch: Sense of hearing.</td></tr><tr><td>Glossopharyngeal</td><td>IX</td><td>Mixed</td><td>Produces the gag and swallowing reflexes. Taste (posterior third of the tongue).</td></tr><tr><td>Vagus</td><td>X</td><td>Mixed</td><td>Innervates muscles of throat and mouth for swallowing and talking. Other branches responsible for pressor receptors and chemoreceptor activity.</td></tr><tr><td>Accessory</td><td>XI</td><td>Motor</td><td>Movement of the trapezius and sternocleidomastoid muscles.
