<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-vascular-disorders">1. VASCULAR DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-vascular-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Cerebrovascular disorders (CVA) is an umbrella term that refers to any functional abnormality of the central nervous system (CNS) that occurs when the normal blood supply to the brain is disrupted.</li>
<li>These disorders are also referred to as stroke.</li>
</ul>
<p>CVA can be divided into two major categories:</p>
<ul>
<li>Ischemic stroke; accounts for 85% of all CVA cases. There is vascular occlusion and significant hypo perfusion of the brain tissue.</li>
<li>Hemorrhagic stroke; accounts for 15% of all CVA cases. There is extravasation of blood into the brain tissue or subarachnoid space.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="ischemic-stroke">ISCHEMIC STROKE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ischemic-stroke" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>It refers to a sudden loss of function of the brain tissue resulting from disruption of the blood supply to a part of the brain. This event is usually the result of long-standing cerebrovascular disease.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="aetiology">AETIOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aetiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The cause of ischemic stroke is mainly formation of a thrombus in the blood vessels occluding the blood flow to the brain.</p>
<p>Based on the cause, ischemic stroke can be subdivided into 5 categories:</p>
<ol>
<li>Large artery thrombotic stroke: They are due to atherosclerotic plaques in the large blood vessels of the brain leading to ischemia and infarction.</li>
<li>Small penetrating artery thrombosis; affect one or more vessels and are the most common type of ischemic stroke.</li>
<li>Cardiogenic embolic; They are associated with cardiac dysrhythmias, usually atrial fibrillation. Emboli originate from the heart and circulate to the cerebral vasculature, most commonly the left middle cerebral artery, resulting in a stroke.</li>
<li>Cryptogenic strokes, which have no known cause</li>
<li>Other strokes, from causes such as cocaine use, coagulopathies, migraine etc.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>In an ischemic brain attack, there is disruption of the cerebral blood flow due to obstruction of a blood vessel.</li>
<li>This disruption in blood flow initiates a complex series of cellular metabolic events referred to as the ischemic cascade.</li>
<li>The ischemic cascade begins when cerebral blood flow falls to less than 25 mL/100 g/min. At this point, neurons can no longer maintain aerobic respiration.</li>
<li>The mitochondria must then switch to anaerobic respiration, which generates large amounts of lactic acid, causing a change in the pH level.</li>
<li>This switch to the less efficient anaerobic respiration also renders the neuron incapable of producing sufficient energy needed for cell metabolism and finally the cell ceases to function.</li>
<li>If there is no intervention, the brain cells die leading to brain infarction.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical Manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Numbness or weakness of the face, arm, or leg, especially on one side of the body</li>
<li>Confusion or change in mental status</li>
<li>Trouble speaking or understanding speech</li>
<li>Visual disturbances</li>
<li>Difficulty walking, dizziness, or loss of balance or coordination</li>
<li>Sudden severe headache</li>
<li>There is loss of cognitive, visual, cranial nerves, motor and sensory functioning.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="visual-field-deficits">Visual Field Deficits<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#visual-field-deficits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Hemianopsia (loss of half of the visual field)</li>
<li>Loss of peripheral vision</li>
<li>Diplopia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="motor-deficits">Motor Deficits<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#motor-deficits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Hemiparesis</li>
<li>Hemiplegia</li>
<li>Ataxia</li>
<li>Dysphagia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="sensory-deficits">Sensory Deficits<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sensory-deficits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Paresthesia (occurs on the side opposite the lesion)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="verbal-deficits">Verbal Deficits<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#verbal-deficits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Expressive aphasia</li>
<li>Receptive aphasia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="cognitive-deficits">Cognitive Deficits<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cognitive-deficits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Short- and long-term memory loss</li>
<li>Decreased attention span</li>
</ul>
<p>COLLINS &amp; BOSCO [KMTC NRB CAMPUS. MAR &amp; SEPT 2020] NEUROLOGICAL NURSING</p>
<ul>
<li>Impaired ability to concentrate</li>
<li>Poor abstract reasoning</li>
<li>Altered judgment</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Emotional Deficits</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Loss of self-control</li>
<li>Emotional instability</li>
<li>Decreased tolerance to stressful situations</li>
<li>Depression</li>
<li>Withdrawal</li>
<li>Fear, hostility, and anger</li>
<li>Feelings of isolation</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Assessment and Diagnostic Findings</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Complete history taking</li>
<li>Physical and neurologic examination.</li>
<li>Initial assessment focuses on airway patency, respiratory function and cardiovascular Status.</li>
<li>Diagnostic tests such as CT scan to determine if stroke is ischemic or hemorrhagic.</li>
<li>Other tests include ECG, Cerebral angiography and transcranial doppler studies.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>RISK FACTORS</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Advanced age, gender, and race are well-known non-modifiable risk factors for stroke.</li>
<li>Modifiable risk factors include:</li>
<li>hypertension, cardiovascular disease,</li>
<li>high cholesterol, obesity,</li>
<li>diabetes</li>
<li>Oral contraceptive use (increases risk, especially with coexisting hypertension, smoking, and high estrogen levels)</li>
<li>Smoking</li>
<li>Drug abuse (especially cocaine)</li>
<li>Excessive alcohol consumption</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>MEDICAL MANAGEMENT</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Platelet-inhibiting medications (aspirin, dipyridamole, clopidogrel and ticlopidine decrease the incidence of cerebral infarction in patients who have experienced CVA from suspected embolic or thrombotic causes.)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Use of Thrombolytic therapy; Recombinant tissue plasminogen activator (t-PA) is a genetically engineered form of t-PA, a thrombolytic substance made naturally by the body.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It works by binding to fibrin and converting plasminogen to plasmin, which stimulates fibrinolysis of the atherosclerotic lesion.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The patient is weighed to determine the dose of t-PA.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The minimum dose is 0.9 mg/kg; the maximum dose is 90 mg.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The patient is admitted to the intensive care unit, where continuous cardiac monitoring is implemented.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Vital signs are obtained every 15 minutes for the first 2 hours, every 30 minutes for the next 6 hours, then every hour for 16 hours.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Airway management is instituted based on the patients clinical condition and arterial blood gas values.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>THERAPY FOR PATIENTS WITH ISCHEMIC STROKE NOT RECEIVING t-PA</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Anticoagulant administration (IV heparin or low-molecular-weight heparin) for ischemic strokes and careful maintenance of cerebral hemodynamics to maintain cerebral perfusion is done.</li>
<li>Measures to reduce ICP, such as administering an osmotic diuretic (eg, mannitol), maintaining PaCO2 within the normal range.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Other treatment measures include:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Elevation of the head of the bed to promote venous drainage and to lower increased ICP</li>
<li>Intubation with an endotracheal tube to establish a patent airway, if necessary.</li>
<li>Continuous hemodynamic monitoring. Systolic pressure should be maintained at less than 180 mm Hg, diastolic pressure at less than 100 mm Hg.</li>
<li>Continuous neurologic assessment to determine whether the stroke is evolving or whether other acute complications are developing, such as bleeding from anticoagulants medication.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>NURSING PROCESS: ASESSEMENT.</strong>
Assess for;</p>
<ul>
<li>Change in the level of consciousness or responsiveness as evidenced by movement,</li>
</ul>
<p>37</p>
<p>COLLINS &amp; BOSCO [KMTC NRB CAMPUS. MAR &amp; SEPT 2020] NEUROLOGICAL NURSING</p>
<p>resistance to changes of position, and response to stimulation; orientation to time, place, and person</p>
<ul>
<li>Presence or absence of voluntary or involuntary movements of the extremities; muscle tone; body posture; and position of the head</li>
<li>Stiffness or flaccidity of the neck</li>
<li>Eye opening, comparative size of pupils and pupillary reactions to light, and ocular position</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-diagnosis">Nursing Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Impaired physical mobility related to hemiparesis, loss of balance and coordination, spasticity, and brain injury</li>
<li>Acute pain (painful shoulder) related to hemiplegia and disuse</li>
<li>Self-care deficits (hygiene, toileting, grooming, and feeding) related to stroke sequelae</li>
<li>Disturbed sensory perception related to altered sensory reception, transmission, and/or integration</li>
<li>Incontinence related to flaccid bladder, confusion, or difficulty in communicating.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="potential-complication">Potential Complication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#potential-complication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Inadequate oxygen delivery to the brain</li>
<li>Pneumonia</li>
<li>Hemorrhagic Stroke</li>
<li>Hemorrhagic strokes account for 15% of cerebrovascular disorders and are primarily caused by an intracranial or subarachnoid hemorrhage.</li>
<li>Hemorrhagic strokes are caused by bleeding into the brain tissue, the ventricles, or the subarachnoid space.</li>
<li>Primary intracerebral hemorrhage from a spontaneous rupture of small vessels accounts for approximately 80% of hemorrhagic strokes and is primarily caused by uncontrolled hypertension</li>
<li>Secondary intracerebral hemorrhage is associated with arteriovenous malformations (AVMs), intracranial aneurysms, or certain medications (eg, anticoagulants and amphetamines)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="intracranial-cerebral-aneurysm">INTRACRANIAL (CEREBRAL) ANEURYSM:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#intracranial-cerebral-aneurysm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>An intracranial (cerebral) aneurysm is a dilation of the walls of a cerebral artery that develops as a result of weakness in the arterial wall. The cause is unknown, although research is ongoing.</li>
<li>An aneurysm may be due to atherosclerosis, resulting in a defect in the vessel wall with subsequent weakness of the wall, a congenital defect of the vessel wall, hypertensive vascular disease, head trauma, or advancing age</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical Manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Many of the same motor, sensory, cranial nerve, cognitive, and other functions that are disrupted following ischemic stroke are altered following a hemorrhagic stroke.</li>
<li>In addition to that, Rupture of an aneurysm or AVM (arteriovenous malformation) usually produces a sudden, unusually severe headache and often loss of consciousness for a variable period.</li>
<li>There may be pain and rigidity of the back of the neck (nuchal rigidity) and spine due to meningeal irritation.</li>
<li>Visual disturbances (visual loss, diplopia, ptosis) occur when the aneurysm is adjacent to the oculomotor nerve.</li>
<li>Tinnitus, dizziness, and hemiparesis may also occur.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="medical-management">Medical Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The goals of medical treatment of hemorrhagic stroke are:</li>
<li> To allow the brain to recover from the initial insult (bleeding),</li>
<li> To prevent or minimize the risk for rebleeding, and</li>
<li> To prevent or treat complications</li>
<li>Management consists of bed rest with sedation to prevent agitation and stress,</li>
<li>Management of vasospasm, and surgical or medical treatment to prevent rebleeding.</li>
<li>Analgesics (codeine, acetaminophen) are prescribed for head and neck pain.</li>
<li>The patient is fitted with elastic compression stockings to prevent deep vein thrombosis, a threat to any patient on bed rest.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="potential-complications">Potential Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#potential-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Rebleeding</li>
<li>Cerebral vasospasm resulting in cerebral ischemia;</li>
<li>Acute hydrocephalus</li>
<li>Seizures</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="surgical-management">Surgical Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surgical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The goal of surgery is to prevent bleeding in an unruptured aneurysm and further bleeding in an already ruptured aneurysm.</li>
</ul>
<p>38</p>
<p>COLLINS &amp; BOSCO [KMTC NRB CAMPUS. MAR &amp; SEPT 2020] NEUROLOGICAL NURSING</p>
<ul>
<li>This objective is accomplished by isolating the aneurysm from its circulation or by strengthening the arterial wall.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-process">NURSING PROCESS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A complete neurologic assessment is performed initially and should include evaluation for the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Altered level of consciousness</li>
<li>Sluggish pupillary reaction</li>
<li>Motor and sensory dysfunction</li>
<li>Cranial nerve deficits (extraocular eye movements, facial droop, presence of ptosis)</li>
<li>Speech difficulties and visual disturbance</li>
<li>Headache and nuchal rigidity or other neurologic deficits</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-diagnoses">NURSING DIAGNOSES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-diagnoses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Ineffective cerebral tissue perfusion related to bleeding.</li>
<li>Disturbed sensory perception related to medically imposed restrictions (aneurysm precautions)</li>
<li>Anxiety related to illness and/or medically imposed restrictions (aneurysm precautions)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aneurysm-precautions">Aneurysm Precautions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aneurysm-precautions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The patient is placed on immediate and absolute bed rest in a quiet, non-stressful environment because activity, pain, and anxiety elevate the blood pressure, which increases the risk for bleeding.</li>
<li>The head of the bed is elevated 15 to 30 degrees to promote venous drainage and decrease ICP.</li>
<li>Thigh-high elastic compression stockings are prescribed to decrease the incidence of deep vein thrombosis resulting from immobility.</li>
<li>The nurse administers all personal care. The patient is fed and bathed to prevent any exertion that might raise the blood pressure.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-patients-with-neurologic-trauma">MANAGEMENT OF PATIENTS WITH NEUROLOGIC TRAUMA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-patients-with-neurologic-trauma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-head-injuries">2. HEAD INJURIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-head-injuries" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Head injury is a broad classification that includes injury to the scalp, skull, or brain.</li>
<li>It is the most common cause of death from trauma.</li>
<li>Damage to the brain from traumatic injury takes two forms: primary injury and secondary injury.</li>
<li>Primary injury is the initial damage to the brain that results from the traumatic event. This may include contusions, lacerations, and torn blood vessels from impact, acceleration/deceleration, or foreign object penetration.</li>
<li>Secondary injury evolves over the ensuing hours and days after the initial injury and is due primarily to brain swelling or ongoing bleeding</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Brain suffers traumatic injury</li>
<li>Brain swelling or bleeding increases intracranial volume</li>
<li>Rigid cranium allows no room for expansion of contents so intracranial pressure increases</li>
<li>Pressure on blood vessels within the brain causes blood flow to the brain to slow</li>
<li>Cerebral hypoxia and ischemia occur</li>
<li>Intracranial pressure continues to rise. Brain may herniate</li>
<li>Cerebral blood flow ceases</li>
<li>Brain death</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-brain-injuries">TYPES OF BRAIN INJURIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-brain-injuries" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="concussion">Concussion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#concussion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>A cerebral concussion is a minor head injury characterised by temporary loss of neurologic function with no apparent structural damage.</li>
<li>The jarring of the brain may be so slight as to cause only dizziness and spots before the eyes ("seeing stars"), or it may be severe enough to cause complete loss of consciousness for a few seconds.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="contusion">Contusion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contusion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Cerebral contusion is a more severe injury in which the brain is bruised, with possible surface hemorrhage.</li>
<li>The patient is unconscious for more than a few seconds or minutes.</li>
<li>Clinical signs and symptoms depend on the size of the contusion and the amount of associated cerebral edema.</li>
</ul>
<p>COLLINS &amp; BOSCO [KMTC NRB CAMPUS. MAR &amp; SEPT 2020] NEUROLOGICAL NURSING</p>
<ul>
<li>The patient may lie motionless, with a faint pulse, shallow respirations, and cool, pale skin.</li>
<li>Often there is involuntary evacuation of the bowels and the bladder.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="intracranial-hemorrhage">Intracranial Hemorrhage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#intracranial-hemorrhage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A severe form of brain injuries leading to formation of hematomas.</li>
<li>Hematomas (collections of blood) that develop within the cranial vault are the most serious brain injuries.</li>
<li>A hematoma may be epidural (above the dura), subdural (below the dura), or intracerebral (within the brain).</li>
<li>Major symptoms are frequently delayed until the hematoma is large enough to cause distortion of the brain and increased ICP.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-manifestations-of-head-injuries">Clinical Manifestations Of Head Injuries<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations-of-head-injuries" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Altered level of consciousness</li>
<li>Confusion</li>
<li>Pupillary abnormalities (changes in shape, size, and response to light)</li>
<li>Altered or absent gag reflex</li>
<li>Absent corneal reflex</li>
<li>Sudden onset of neurologic deficits</li>
<li>Changes in vital signs (altered respiratory pattern, hypertension, bradycardia, tachycardia, hypothermia or hyperthermia)</li>
<li>Vision and hearing impairment</li>
<li>Sensory dysfunction</li>
<li>Spasticity</li>
<li>Headache</li>
<li>Vertigo</li>
<li>Movement disorders</li>
<li>Seizures</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="assessment-and-diagnostic-findings">Assessment and Diagnostic Findings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment-and-diagnostic-findings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Physical and neurologic examinations are done.</li>
<li>CT and MRI are the primary neuroimaging diagnostic tools and are useful in evaluating soft tissue injuries.</li>
<li>Positron emission tomography (PET scan) is done to examine the brain functioning.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>NB</strong>: Any individual with a head injury is presumed to have a cervical spine injury until proven otherwise. From the scene of the injury, the patient is transported on a board with the head and neck maintained in alignment with the axis of the body.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="medical-management">Medical Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>As the damaged brain swells with edema or as blood collects within the brain, a rise in ICP occurs; Review management of increased ICP.</li>
<li>Surgery is required for evacuation of blood clots, dbridement and elevation of depressed fractures of the skull, and suture of severe scalp lacerations</li>
<li>Treatment also includes ventilatory support.</li>
<li>Seizure prevention by administering antiseizure drugs</li>
<li>Fluid and electrolyte maintenance,</li>
<li>Nutritional support.</li>
<li>Pain and anxiety management.</li>
<li>Comatose patients are intubated and mechanically ventilated to ensure adequate oxygenation and protect the airway.</li>
<li>A nasogastric tube may be inserted because reduced gastric motility and reverse peristalsis are associated with head injury, making regurgitation and aspiration common in the first few hours.</li>
<li>Incase of brain death, the nurse may provide information to the family and get consent for potential organ donation.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-process">NURSING PROCESS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="assessment">Assessment;<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Take a health history to include the following questions:</li>
<li> When did the injury occur?</li>
<li> What caused the injury? A high-velocity missile? An object striking the head? A fall?</li>
<li> What was the direction and force of the blow?</li>
<li>A complete neurological examination is done.</li>
<li>Physical assessment</li>
<li>Assess for the level of consciousness using a Glasgow coma scale.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-diagnoses">NURSING DIAGNOSES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-diagnoses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li> Ineffective airway clearance and impaired gas exchange related to brain injury</li>
<li> Ineffective cerebral tissue perfusion related to increased ICP.</li>
<li> Deficient fluid volume related to decreased LOC and hormonal dysfunction</li>
<li> Imbalanced nutrition, less than body requirements, related to metabolic changes, fluid restriction, and inadequate intake</li>
</ul>
<p>COLLINS &amp; BOSCO [KMTC NRB CAMPUS. MAR &amp; SEPT 2020] NEUROLOGICAL NURSING</p>
<p> Risk for injury (self-directed and directed at others) related to seizures, disorientation, restlessness, or brain damage
 Potential for impaired skin integrity related to bed rest, hemiparesis, hemiplegia, and immobility
 Disturbed thought processes (deficits in intellectual function, communication, memory, information processing) related to brain injury</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="potential-complications">Potential Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#potential-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Cerebral edema and herniation</li>
<li>Impaired oxygenation and ventilation</li>
<li>Post-traumatic seizures.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-spinal-cord-injury">3. SPINAL CORD INJURY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-spinal-cord-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Spinal cord injury (SCI) is a major health problem.</li>
<li>SCI occurs almost four times more often in males than females.</li>
<li>The predominant risk factors for SCI include age, gender, and alcohol and drug use.</li>
<li>The vertebrae most frequently involved in SCI are the 5th, 6th, and 7th cervical (neck), the 12th thoracic, and the 1st lumbar vertebrae</li>
<li>These vertebrae are the most susceptible because there is a greater range of mobility in the vertebral column in these areas.</li>
<li>SCIs can be separated into two categories: primary injuries and secondary injuries.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical Manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A complete spinal cord lesion can result in paraplegia (paralysis of the lower body) or quadriplegia (paralysis of all four extremities). There is no motor or sensory function that is preserved.</li>
<li>Incomplete spinal cord lesions are classified according to the area of spinal cord damage. Motor and sensory function is preserved below the neurologic level.</li>
<li>If conscious, the patient usually complains of acute pain in the back or neck.</li>
<li>Respiratory dysfunction is related to the level of injury.</li>
<li>The muscles contributing to respiration are the abdominals and intercostals (T1 to T11) and the diaphragm.</li>
<li>In high cervical cord injury, acute respiratory failure is the leading cause of death.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="assessment-and-diagnostic-findings">Assessment and Diagnostic Findings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment-and-diagnostic-findings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>A detailed neurologic examination is performed.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Diagnostic x-rays (lateral cervical spine x-rays) and CT scanning are performed initially.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An MRI scan may be ordered as a further workup if a ligamentous injury is suspected</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="emergency-management">Emergency Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#emergency-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The immediate management of the patient at the scene of the injury is critical, because improper handling can cause further damage and loss of neurologic function.</li>
<li>At the scene of the injury, the patient must be immobilized on a spinal (back) board, with head and neck in a neutral position, to prevent an incomplete injury from becoming complete.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-spinal-cord-injuries">Management of Spinal Cord Injuries<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-spinal-cord-injuries" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The patient is resuscitated as necessary, and oxygenation and cardiovascular stability are maintained.</li>
<li>Administration of high-dose corticosteroids, specifically methylprednisolone, has been found to improve motor and sensory outcomes.</li>
<li>If endotracheal intubation is necessary, extreme care is taken to avoid flexing or extending the patient's neck, which can result in an extension of a cervical injury.</li>
<li>Management of SCI requires immobilization and reduction of dislocations (restoration of normal position) and stabilization of the vertebral column.</li>
<li>Cervical fractures are reduced and the cervical spine is aligned with some form of skeletal traction, such as skeletal tongs or calipers.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="surgical-management">Surgical Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surgical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Surgery is indicated in any of the following instances:</p>
<ul>
<li>Compression of the cord is evident.</li>
<li>The injury results in a fragmented or unstable vertebral body.</li>
<li>The injury involves a wound that penetrates the cord.</li>
<li>There are bony fragments in the spinal canal.</li>
<li>The patient's neurologic status is deteriorating.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="possible-complications">Possible Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#possible-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Neurogenic shock</li>
<li>Deep venous Thrombosis</li>
<li>Respiratory failure</li>
<li>Pneumonia</li>
<li>Autonomic dysreflexia</li>
</ul>
<p>COLLINS &amp; BOSCO [KMTC NRB CAMPUS. MAR &amp; SEPT 2020] NEUROLOGICAL NURSING</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-process">NURSING PROCESS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="assessment">Assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>The breathing pattern is observed, the strength of the cough is assessed, and the lungs are auscultated, because paralysis of abdominal and respiratory muscles diminishes coughing and makes it difficult to clear bronchial and pharyngeal secretions.</li>
<li>The patient is monitored closely for any changes in motor or sensory function and for symptoms of progressive neurologic damage.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-diagnoses">NURSING DIAGNOSES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-diagnoses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li> Ineffective breathing patterns related to weakness or paralysis of abdominal and intercostal muscles and inability to clear secretions</li>
<li> Ineffective airway clearance related to weakness of intercostal muscles</li>
<li> Impaired physical mobility related to motor and sensory impairment</li>
<li> Disturbed sensory perception related to motor and sensory impairment</li>
<li> Risk for impaired skin integrity related to immobility and sensory loss</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-management-of-patients-with-neurologic-infections">4. MANAGEMENT OF PATIENTS WITH NEUROLOGIC INFECTIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-management-of-patients-with-neurologic-infections" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="meningitis">MENINGITIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#meningitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Meningitis is an inflammation of the meninges, the protective membranes that surround the brain and spinal cord.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Meningitis is classified as aseptic or septic.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In aseptic meningitis, bacteria are not the cause of the inflammation; the cause is viral or secondary to lymphoma, leukemia, or brain abscess.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Septic meningitis refers to meningitis caused by bacteria, most commonly <em>Neisseria meningitidis</em>, although <em>Haemophilus influenzae</em> and <em>Streptococcus pneumoniae</em> are also causative agents.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="predisposing-factors">Predisposing Factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Overcrowding</li>
<li>Tobacco use</li>
<li>Viral upper respiratory</li>
<li>Otitis media and mastoiditis</li>
<li>Immunosuppression.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Meningeal infections generally originate in one of two ways:</li>
<li>-through the bloodstream as a consequence of other infections, or</li>
<li>-by direct extension, such as might occur after a traumatic injury to the facial bones, or secondary to invasive procedures.</li>
<li><em>N. meningitidis</em> concentrates in the nasopharynx and is transmitted by secretion or aerosol contamination.</li>
<li>Once the causative organism enters the bloodstream, it crosses the blood-brain barrier and causes an inflammatory reaction in the meninges.</li>
<li>Independent of the causative agent, inflammation of the subarachnoid space and pia mater occurs.</li>
<li>Since there is little room for expansion within the cranial vault, the inflammation may cause increased intracranial pressure.</li>
<li>(CSF) flows in the subarachnoid space, where inflammatory cellular material from the affected meningeal tissue enters and accumulates in the subarachnoid space, thereby increasing the CSF cell count</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical Manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Headache and fever are frequently the initial symptoms.</li>
<li>Fever tends to remain high throughout the course of the illness.</li>
<li>Nuchal rigidity (stiff neck) is an early sign. Any attempts at flexion of the head are difficult because of spasms in the muscles of the neck. Forceful flexion causes severe pain.</li>
<li>Positive Kernigs sign: When the patient is lying with the thigh flexed on the abdomen, the leg cannot be completely extended</li>
<li>Positive Brudzinskis sign: When the patients neck is flexed, flexion of the knees and hips is produced; when passive flexion of the lower extremity of one side is made, a similar movement is seen in the opposite extremity.</li>
<li>Photophobia: (extreme sensitivity to light).</li>
<li>A rash can be a striking feature of <em>N. meningitidis</em> infection.</li>
<li>Disorientation and memory impairment are common early in the course of the illness</li>
<li>Seizures and increased intracranial pressure (ICP) are also associated with meningitis</li>
</ul>
<p>COLLINS &amp; BOSCO [KMTC NRB CAMPUS. MAR &amp; SEPT 2020] NEUROLOGICAL NURSING</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="assessment-and-diagnostic-findings">Assessment and Diagnostic Findings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment-and-diagnostic-findings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Lumbar puncture is the main diagnostic test to obtain CSF for culture and Gram staining to identify the causative organism.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="medical-management">Medical Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Early administration of an antibiotic that crosses the blood-brain barrier into the subarachnoid space in sufficient concentration to halt the multiplication of bacteria.</li>
<li>Penicillin antibiotics (eg, ampicillin, piperacillin) or one of the cephalosporins (eg, ceftriaxone sodium, cefotaxime sodium) are used.</li>
<li>Vancomycin hydrochloride alone or in combination with rifampin may be used if resistant strains of bacteria are identified.</li>
<li>Dexamethasone has been shown to be beneficial as adjunct therapy in the treatment of acute bacterial meningitis.</li>
<li>Dehydration and shock are treated with fluid volume expanders.</li>
<li>Seizures, which may occur in the early course of the disease, are controlled with phenytoin (Dilantin).</li>
<li>Increased ICP is treated as necessary</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-management">Nursing Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Neurologic status and vital signs are continually assessed.</li>
<li>Pulse oximetry and arterial blood gas values are used to quickly identify the need for respiratory support as the increasing ICP compromises the brain stem.</li>
<li>Insertion of a cuffed endotracheal tube (or tracheotomy) and mechanical ventilation may be necessary to maintain adequate tissue oxygenation</li>
<li>Intravenous(IV) fluid replacement may be prescribed, but care is taken not to increase the ICP.</li>
<li>Fevers are managed with antipyretics</li>
<li>Protecting the patient from injury secondary to seizure activity or altered level of consciousness</li>
<li>Preventing complications associated with immobility, such as pressure ulcers and pneumonia</li>
<li>Instituting droplet precautions until 24 hours after the initiation of antibiotic therapy</li>
<li>An important aspect of the nurse's role is to support the patient and to assist the family in identifying others who can be supportive to them during the crisis.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="brain-abscess">BRAIN ABSCESS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#brain-abscess" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A brain abscess is a collection of infectious material within the tissue of the brain.</li>
<li>It may occur by direct invasion of the brain from intracranial trauma or surgery; by spread of infection from nearby sites, such as the sinuses, ears, and teeth.</li>
<li>To prevent brain abscess, otitis media, mastoiditis, sinusitis, dental infections, and systemic infections should be treated promptly.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical Manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Headache, usually worse in the morning, is the most prevailing symptom.</li>
<li>Vomiting.</li>
<li>Focal neurologic signs (weakness of an extremity, decreasing vision, seizures) may occur, depending on the site of the abscess.</li>
<li>Changes in mental status, as reflected in lethargic, confused, irritable, or disoriented behavior.</li>
<li>Fever may or may not be present.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="assessment-and-diagnostic-findings">Assessment and Diagnostic Findings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment-and-diagnostic-findings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A computed tomography (CT) scan is invaluable in locating the site of the abscess.</li>
<li>A magnetic resonance imaging (MRI) scan is also useful.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="medical-management">Medical Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Brain abscess is treated with antimicrobial therapy and surgical incision or aspiration.</li>
<li>Penicillin G (20 million U) and chloramphenicol (4 to 6 g/day given intravenously in divided doses) are given.</li>
<li>Corticosteroids may be prescribed to help reduce the inflammatory cerebral edema if the patient shows evidence of an increasing neurologic deficit.</li>
<li>Antiseizure medications (phenytoin, phenobarbital) may be prescribed to prevent seizures</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-management">Nursing Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Ongoing neurologic assessment alerts the nurse to changes in ICP.</li>
<li>Patient safety is also a key nursing responsibility. Injury may result from decreased level of consciousness and falls related to motor weakness or seizures.</li>
<li>The nurse must assess the family's ability to express their distress at the patient's condition, cope with</li>
</ul>
<p>COLLINS &amp; BOSCO [KMTC NRB CAMPUS. MAR &amp; SEPT 2020] NEUROLOGICAL NURSING</p>
<p>the patient's illness and deficits, and obtain support.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="encephalitis">ENCEPHALITIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#encephalitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Encephalitis is an acute inflammatory process of the brain tissue.</li>
<li>Herpes simplex virus (HSV) is the most common cause of acute encephalitis.</li>
<li>The initial symptoms include fever, headache, confusion, and behavioral abnormalities</li>
<li>Focal neurologic symptoms reflect the areas of cerebral inflammation and necrosis and include behavioral change, focal seizures, dysphasia, hemiparesis, and altered level of consciousness.</li>
<li>Neuroimaging studies, electroencephalography (EEG), and CSF examination are used to diagnose HSV encephalitis.</li>
<li>Acyclovir, an antiviral agent, is the medication of choice in HSV treatment.</li>
<li>Other causes of encephalitis are Fungal and Arthropod borne encephalitis.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="spinal-disc-problems">SPINAL DISC PROBLEMS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#spinal-disc-problems" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Disorders affecting intervertebral discs include disc herniation (prolapsed intervertebral disc), degenerative disc disease and infection (discitis).</li>
<li>Spinal disc problems can lead to symptoms of back pain and/or sciatica. There are many other causes of back pain and/or sciatica but they do not primarily originate from the intervertebral discs.</li>
<li>Back pain with/without sciatica is extremely common. Most may be classified as 'simple' back pain where serious underlying pathology is unlikely. However, it is essential always to be aware of 'red flag' warning signs which may merit investigations or even emergency admission.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="spinal-anatomy">Spinal anatomy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#spinal-anatomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The spinal cord is shorter than the spinal canal. The spinal cord ends between the L1 and L2 vertebrae in adults and between L2 and L3 in children. Below the termination of the spinal cord, the nerve roots form the cauda equina which has a horse-tail like appearance. The cauda equina contains the nerve roots L1-L5 and S1-S5. Spinal pathology below L1 of the vertebral column produces mostly lower motor neurone signs.</p>
<p>The intervertebral discs lie between adjacent vertebrae. They consist of a peripheral fibrocartilaginous part called the annulus fibrosus and a central semifluid/gelatinous part - the nucleus pulposus.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="when-to-refer-someone-with-low-back-pain-sciatica">When to refer someone with low back pain/sciatica<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#when-to-refer-someone-with-low-back-pain-sciatica" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Arrange emergency referral to a spinal surgery service if there is suspicion of:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cauda equina syndrome.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Acute spinal cord compression: new/progressive widespread neurological deficit.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Progressive limb weakness including major motor radiculopathy.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Arrange urgent referral to a spinal surgery service or urgent MRI (within two weeks) if:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>There is suspicion of tumour or infection.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Red flags are present in the absence of neurological dysfunction.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Seek advice from the emergency spinal surgery service for people with severe or progressive motor deficit (for example, foot drop).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Consider offering referral:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>For a group exercise programme.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To a physiotherapist, but only as part of a treatment package including exercise with or without psychological therapy.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>For psychological therapies using a cognitive behavioural approach, but only as part of a treatment package including exercise, with or without manual therapy.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prolapsed-intervertebral-disc">PROLAPSED INTERVERTEBRAL DISC<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prolapsed-intervertebral-disc" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The nucleus pulposus of the spinal disc is usually contained by the annulus fibrosus. If the nucleus herniates, it can irritate and/or compress the adjacent nerve root, causing symptoms of sciatica.</li>
<li>Traumatic disc herniation can occur. Spinal disc herniation can also occur secondary to degenerative disc disease.</li>
<li>A herniated nucleus pulposus is most common in those aged below 40 years, whilst degeneration of discs tends to affect those aged over 40 years, with the prevalence increasing with advancing age. Spinal disc lesions of the lumbar spine are more common than those of the cervical spine and disc lesions of the thoracic spine are rare.</li>
<li>The term sciatica is used for the pain, tingling and numbness that arise due to nerve root entrapment</li>
</ul>
<p>COLLINS &amp; BOSCO [KMTC NRB CAMPUS. MAR &amp; SEPT 2020] NEUROLOGICAL NURSING</p>
<p>in the lumbosacral spine. The symptoms may be felt in one or more of the lumbar nerve roots. About 90% of cases of sciatica are caused by a herniated intervertebral disc. This most commonly occurs at the L5/S1 level.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="above-and-side-views">Above and side views<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#above-and-side-views" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-d41b868d.jpeg" alt="img-42.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lumbosacral-disc-herniation">Lumbosacral disc herniation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lumbosacral-disc-herniation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>If there is nerve entrapment in the lumbosacral spine, this leads to symptoms of sciatica which include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Unilateral leg pain which radiates below the knee to the foot/toes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The leg pain being more severe than the back pain.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Numbness, paraesthesia, weakness and/or loss of tendon reflexes, which may be present and are found in the same distribution and only in one nerve root distribution.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A positive straight leg raising test (there is greater leg pain and/or more nerve compression symptoms on raising the leg).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pain which is usually relieved by lying down and exacerbated by long walks and prolonged sitting.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Large herniations can compress the cauda equina, leading to symptoms/signs of saddle anaesthesia, urinary retention and incontinence as described above.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Symptoms tend at least to resolve partially in 66% of people with a disc herniation, after six months. This is because the herniated portion tends to regress over time.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>However, nerve root compression can lead to permanent nerve damage with sensory and motor deficit.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="thoracic-disc-herniation">Thoracic disc herniation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#thoracic-disc-herniation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Spinal disc problems in the thoracic spine can lead either to nerve root irritation or to cord compression.</li>
<li>Thoracic spine lesions can present with symptoms similar to lumbar disc lesions.</li>
<li>In nerve root irritation, there may be shooting pain down the legs.</li>
<li>There may be pain, paraesthesia or dysaesthesia in a dermatomal distribution.</li>
<li>A thoraco-abdominal sensory examination can help to determine the level of the lesion: the nipple is innervated by T4; the xiphoid by T7; the umbilicus by T10; the inguinal region by T12.</li>
<li>Testing of the abdominal and cremasteric reflexes can help to identify myelopathy and cord compression.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cord-compression">Cord compression:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cord-compression" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>This is a neurosurgical emergency.</li>
<li>Cord compression in the thoracic spine can produce paraplegia.</li>
<li>There may be clonus or a positive Babinski reflex.</li>
<li>There may be bladder/bowel dysfunction.</li>
<li>Herniation of T2-T5 can mimic cervical disc disease.</li>
</ul>
