<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical Manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Depending on the location of the discharging neurons, seizures may range from a simple staring episode to prolonged convulsive movements with loss of consciousness.</li>
<li>The initial pattern of the seizures indicates the region of the brain in which the seizure originates.</li>
<li>In simple partial seizures, only a finger or hand may shake, or the mouth may jerk uncontrollably.</li>
<li>In complex partial seizures, the person either remains motionless or moves automatically but inappropriately for time and place, or may experience excessive emotions of fear, anger, or irritability.</li>
<li>There is involvement of more than one part of the brain.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="generalized-seizures">GENERALIZED SEIZURES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#generalized-seizures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Previously referred to as grand mal seizures, involve both hemispheres of the brain, causing both sides of the body to react.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stages-of-grand-mal-seizure">STAGES OF GRAND MAL SEIZURE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stages-of-grand-mal-seizure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Prodrome stage: It occurs days or hours before the seizure activity. It is characterized by irritability or hyperactivity etc.</li>
<li>Aura (warning)stage: It is characterised by certain unusual feelings such as peculiar sensation, funny smell, feeling nauseated, abdominal discomfort (gastric secretions) and flashing light.</li>
<li>Tonic stage: It usually lasts about 10 to 20 seconds.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>All muscles become rigid, eyelids open, eyes look up and respiration stops temporarily resulting in cyanosis.</li>
<li>The tongue is bitten causing bleeding, which can be seen from the mouth.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>Clonic stage: It usually lasts about 30 seconds.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>It begins with muscle relaxation, which completely interrupts tonic muscle contraction.</li>
<li>There are brief violent muscle spasms of the whole body, frothing of the mouth and</li>
</ul>
<p>75</p>
<p>COLLINS &amp; BOSCO [KMTC NRB CAMPUS. MAR &amp; SEPT 2020] NEUROLOGICAL NURSING</p>
<p>incontinence of urine and sometimes faeces as well.</p>
<p>5.Ictal phase: The patient goes into deep coma for minutes or hours
6. Post ictal stage:(after the seizure).This is recovery stage, the patient starts regaining consciousness.</p>
<ul>
<li>The patient is often confused and hard to arouse and may sleep for hours.</li>
<li>Many patients complain of headache, sore muscles, fatigue, and depression</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="assessment-and-diagnostic-findings">Assessment and Diagnostic Findings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment-and-diagnostic-findings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A developmental history is taken, including events of pregnancy and childbirth, to seek evidence of preexisting injury.</li>
<li>The patient is also questioned about illnesses or head injuries that may have affected the brain.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnostic-tests-include">DIAGNOSTIC TESTS INCLUDE:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-tests-include" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>MRI is used to detect lesions in the brain and focal abnormalities.</li>
<li>The electroencephalogram (EEG) furnishes diagnostic evidence in a substantial proportion of patients with epilepsy and aids in classifying the type of seizure.</li>
<li>Single photon emission computed tomography (SPECT) is an additional tool sometimes used in the diagnostic workup.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="medical-management">Medical Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Many medications are available to control seizures, although the mechanisms of their actions are still unknown.</li>
<li>The objective is to achieve seizure control with minimal side effects.</li>
<li>Medication therapy controls rather than cures seizures.</li>
<li>Treatment is usually started with a single medication.</li>
<li>The dose and the rate at which the dosage is increased depend on the occurrence of side effects</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="antiseizure-drugs">ANTISEIZURE DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antiseizure-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>carbamazepine (Tegretol) clonazepam (Klonopin)
ethosuximide (Zarontin) felbamate (Felbatol)
gabapentin (Neurotonin) lamotrigine (Lamictal)
levetiracetam (Keppra) oxacarbazepine (Trileptal)
phenobarbital (Luminal) phenytoin (Dilantin)
primidone (Mysoline) tiagabine (Gabitril)
topiramate (Topamax) valproate (Depakote, Depakene)
zonisamide (Zonegran, Excegran)
Review the pharmacology of anti seizure drugs</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects-of-anti-seizure-drugs">SIDE EFFECTS OF ANTI-SEIZURE DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects-of-anti-seizure-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Side effects of antiseizure agents may be divided into three groups:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>idiosyncratic or allergic disorders, which present primarily as skin reactions;</li>
<li>acute toxicity, which may occur when the medication is initially prescribed; or</li>
<li>chronic toxicity, which occurs late in the course of therapy.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="surgical-management">Surgical Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surgical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Surgery is indicated for patients whose epilepsy results from intracranial tumors, abscess, cysts, or vascular anomalies.</li>
<li>Some patients have intractable seizure disorders that do not respond to medication.</li>
<li>There may be a focal atrophic process secondary to trauma, inflammation, stroke, or anoxia.</li>
<li>If the seizures originate in a reasonably well-circumscribed area of the brain that can be excised without producing significant neurologic deficits, the removal of the area generating the seizures may produce long-term control and improvement.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-assessment-during-a-seizure">Nursing Assessment during a Seizure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-assessment-during-a-seizure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A major responsibility of the nurse is to observe and record the sequence of symptoms.</li>
<li>The nature of the seizure usually indicates the type of treatment that is required.</li>
<li>The nurse assesses for the following:</li>
<li>The circumstances before the seizure (visual, auditory, or olfactory stimuli, tactile stimuli,etc)</li>
<li>The occurrence of an aura (visual, auditory, or olfactory)</li>
<li>The first thing the patient does in a seizure</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-care-during-a-seizure">Nursing Care during a Seizure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-during-a-seizure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Provide privacy and protect the patient from curious on-lookers.</li>
<li>[The patient who has an aura [warning of an impending seizure] may have time to seek a safe, private place.]</li>
<li>Ease the patient to the floor, if possible.</li>
<li>Protect the head with a pad to prevent injury (from striking a hard surface).</li>
</ul>
<p>76</p>
<p>COLLINS &amp; BOSCO [KMTC NRB CAMPUS. MAR &amp; SEPT 2020] NEUROLOGICAL NURSING</p>
<ul>
<li>Loosen constrictive clothing.</li>
<li>Push aside any furniture that may injure the patient during the seizure.</li>
<li>If the patient is in bed, remove pillows and raise side rails.</li>
<li>If an aura precedes the seizure, insert an oral airway to reduce the possibility of the tongue or cheek being bitten.</li>
</ul>
<p>NB: Do not attempt to pry open jaws that are clenched in a spasm to insert anything. Broken teeth and injury to the lips and tongue may result from such an action.</p>
<ul>
<li>No attempt should be made to restrain the patient during the seizure because muscular contractions are strong and restraint can produce injury.</li>
<li>If possible, place the patient on one side with head flexed forward, which allows the tongue to fall forward and facilitates drainage of saliva and mucus.</li>
<li>If suction is available, use it if necessary to clear secretions.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-care-after-the-seizure">Nursing Care after the Seizure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-after-the-seizure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Keep the patient on one side to prevent aspiration. Make sure the airway is patent.</li>
<li>There is usually a period of confusion after a grand mal seizure.</li>
<li>A short apneic period may occur during or immediately after a generalized seizure.</li>
<li>The patient, on awakening, should be reoriented to the environment.</li>
<li>If the patient becomes agitated after a seizure (postictal), use calm persuasion and gentle restraint.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-process-assessement">NURSING PROCESS ASSESSEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-process-assessement" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The nurse elicits information about the seizure history.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The patient is asked about the factors or events that may precipitate the seizures.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The nurse determines if the patient has an aura (a premonitory or warning sensation) before an epileptic seizure, which may indicate the origin of the seizure.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The type of movements in the part of the body involved</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The areas of the body involved (turn back bedding to expose patient)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The size of both pupils. Are the eyes open? Did the eyes or head turn to one side?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The presence or absence of automatisms (involuntary motor activity, such as lip smacking or repeated swallowing)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Incontinence of urine or stool</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Duration of each phase of the seizure</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Unconsciousness, if present, and its duration</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Any obvious paralysis or weakness of arms or legs after the seizure</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Inability to speak after the seizure</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Movements at the end of the seizure</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Whether or not the patient sleeps afterward</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cognitive status (confused or not confused) after the seizure</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-diagnoses">NURSING DIAGNOSES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-diagnoses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Risk for injury related to seizure activity</li>
<li>Fear related to the possibility of seizures</li>
<li>Ineffective individual coping related to stresses imposed by epilepsy</li>
<li>Deficient knowledge related to epilepsy and its control</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="potential-complication">Potential Complication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#potential-complication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Status epilepticus</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="status-epilepticus">STATUS EPILEPTICUS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#status-epilepticus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Status epilepticus (acute prolonged seizure activity) is a series of generalized seizures that occur without full recovery of consciousness between attacks.</li>
<li>It is considered a medical emergency.</li>
<li>Status epilepticus produces cumulative effects.</li>
<li>Vigorous muscular contractions impose a heavy metabolic demand and can interfere with respirations.</li>
<li>There is some respiratory arrest at the height of each seizure that produces venous congestion and hypoxia of the brain.</li>
<li>Repeated episodes of cerebral anoxia and edema may lead to irreversible and fatal brain damage.</li>
<li>Factors that precipitate status epilepticus include withdrawal of antiseizure medication, fever, and concurrent infection.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="medical-management">Medical Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The goals of treatment are to stop the seizures as quickly as possible, to ensure adequate cerebral</li>
</ul>
<p>COLLINS &amp; BOSCO [KMTC NRB CAMPUS. MAR &amp; SEPT 2020] NEUROLOGICAL NURSING</p>
<p>oxygenation, and to maintain the patient in a seizure-free state.</p>
<ul>
<li>An airway and adequate oxygenation are established.</li>
<li>If the patient remains unconscious and unresponsive, a cuffed endotracheal tube is inserted.</li>
<li>Intravenous diazepam (Valium), or lorazepam is given slowly in an attempt to halt seizures immediately.</li>
<li>Other medications (phenytoin, phenobarbital) are given later to maintain a seizure-free state.</li>
<li>EEG monitoring may be useful in determining the nature of the seizure activity.</li>
<li>Vital signs and neurologic signs are monitored on a continuing basis.</li>
<li>An intravenous infusion of dextrose is given if the seizure is due to hypoglycemia.</li>
<li>If initial treatment is unsuccessful, general anesthesia with a short-acting barbiturate may be used.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-management">Nursing Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The nurse initiates ongoing assessment and monitoring of respiratory and cardiac function because of the risk for delayed depression of respiration and blood pressure secondary to administration of antiseizure medications and sedatives to halt the seizures.</li>
<li>Nursing assessment also includes monitoring and documenting the seizure activity and the patient's responsiveness.</li>
<li>The patient is turned to a lateral position if possible to assist in draining pharyngeal secretions.</li>
<li>Suction equipment must be available because of the risk for aspiration.</li>
<li>The intravenous line is closely monitored because it may become dislodged during seizures.</li>
<li>Other Nursing interventions are done to the patient during and after seizure as discussed above.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="paediatric-conditions-affecting-the-nervous-system">PAEDIATRIC CONDITIONS AFFECTING THE NERVOUS SYSTEM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#paediatric-conditions-affecting-the-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="hydrocephalus">HYDROCEPHALUS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hydrocephalus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>This is an abnormal condition of fluid around the brain or inside the ventricles.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It is usually a result of an interference with the circulation or absorption of cerebral spinal fluid (CSF).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>There are two distinct types of hydrocephalus according to anatomical positions;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> communicating and</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Non communicating Hydrocephalus.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-communicating-or-extra-ventricular-hydrocephalus">1. Communicating (or Extra Ventricular) Hydrocephalus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-communicating-or-extra-ventricular-hydrocephalus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>In this type of hydrocephalus, the obstruction is outside the ventricular system.</li>
<li>The problem is caused by blockage or occlusion of the sub arachnoid cisterns around the brain stem.</li>
<li>The fluid, which is not being absorbed, compresses the brain and distends the cranial cavity.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<ul>
<li>Subarachnoid haemorrhage</li>
<li>Bacterial meningitis.</li>
<li>Toxoplasmosis</li>
<li>Diseases of the connective tissues</li>
<li>Sardocoidosis (growth of tiny collections of inflammatory cells in different parts of the body)</li>
<li>Head injury</li>
<li>Idiopathic causes</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-non-communicating-hydrocephalus">2. Non Communicating Hydrocephalus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-non-communicating-hydrocephalus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>The obstruction here is within the ventricular systems, leading to interference with the flow of the cerebral spinal fluid to the sub arachnoid space</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<ul>
<li>Congenital defect developmental, for example, Arnold chiari malformation and aqueduct stenosis.</li>
<li>Acquired defects, for example, cerebral abscess, compression of the aqueduct by either aneurysm or haematoma, brain tumour</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="assessement">ASSESSEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessement" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<ul>
<li>A physical assessment should be undertaken to ascertain the extent and seriousness of the condition, taking into account the infant's age and period of onset.</li>
<li>The head circumference (occipito frontal circumference) should be regularly measured.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="management">MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<ul>
<li>Medical treatment with acetazolamide (diamox) is commenced to reduce the production of csf in mild case- hydrocephalus.</li>
</ul>
<p>COLLINS &amp; BOSCO [KMTC NRB CAMPUS. MAR &amp; SEPT 2020] NEUROLOGICAL NURSING</p>
<ul>
<li>Repeated lumbar punctures may be performed to maintain normal cerebral spinal fluid pressure.</li>
</ul>
<p>Surgical intervention may also be undertaken, depending on the severity of the condition.</p>
<ul>
<li>This consists of the removal of obstructions such as tumours, cysts, haemorrhage (haematoma).</li>
<li>A ventriculostomy is done, it involves the destruction of the third and fourth ventricle or the choroid plexus.</li>
<li>A radio opaque ventricular catheter is inserted to shunt cerebro spinal fluid (CSF) from the ventricle to another area outside the central nervous system, for example, the abdominal cavity.</li>
<li>These catheters have valves to prevent flow back of blood or any other secretion into the ventricles.</li>
<li>Types of valves in use are the Spitz Holter valve system, Hakim shunting system and Heyer Schulte Pudenz catheter.</li>
</ul>
<p>Preoperative Nursing Care</p>
<ul>
<li>Monitor signs of increased intracranial pressure and report to the surgeon any changes.</li>
<li>Also, continue to frequently measure the head circumference.</li>
<li>Palpate the fontanelles gently for possible separation of sutures and tension.</li>
<li>Vital signs should be taken and recorded (TPR/BP) every one or two hours.</li>
<li>Any deviations should be reported immediately</li>
<li>The child's behavioural changes, including persistent cries, should be recorded and reported. Regularly change the child's</li>
<li>Two hourly position change in bed is done to prevent bed sores.</li>
<li>The neck should be supported when the child is being moved.</li>
<li>The parents are encouraged to participate in their child's care during their hospital stay and in preparation for discharge.</li>
</ul>
<p>Postoperative Nursing Care</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The preoperative care provided should continue after surgery.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Immediately after surgery, vital signs should be monitored and recorded in one hour intervals, paying particular attention to signs of increasing intracranial pressure.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Other neurological observations, for example, the assessment of the level of consciousness, should also be continued.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The dressings on the operation site is checked regularly.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Always ensure that the child lies on the good side to prevent pressure on the shunt valve.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Careful regular feeds should be given.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Parental education is continued from admission until discharge.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Analgesics and antibiotics are also given.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Post-Operative Complications</p>
<ul>
<li>Meningitis</li>
<li>Vomiting</li>
<li>Infections</li>
</ul>
<p>MICROCEPHALY</p>
<ul>
<li>This is a relatively uncommon congenital condition where there is a defect in the growth of the brain.</li>
<li>The size of the brain becomes three times smaller than normal.</li>
</ul>
<p>Predisposing factors</p>
<ul>
<li>Foetal radiation</li>
<li>Maternal phenylketonuria, which is an inherited metabolic amino acid phenylalanine because the liver has failed to release an enzyme called phenylalaninase</li>
<li>Congenital infections, for example, syphilis, neonatal herpes, rubella</li>
<li>Intrauterine or neonatal anoxia</li>
</ul>
<p>Clinical manifestations</p>
<ul>
<li>The ears are relatively large, the forehead slopes backwards and the head appears smaller.</li>
</ul>
<p>MANAGEMENT</p>
<ul>
<li>There is no treatment available for this condition. Parents are supported and made to understand that.</li>
</ul>
<p>SPINA BIFIDA</p>
<ul>
<li>This is a congenital abnormality, which results from a defect in the formation of the skeletal arch enclosing the spinal cord.</li>
<li>It affects any part of the spinal column and on the skull, but it is more common in the lumbar region.</li>
<li>In spina bifida, the posterior portion of the lamina of one or more vertebrae fails to fuse with or</li>
</ul>
<p>COLLINS &amp; BOSCO [KMTC NRB CAMPUS. MAR &amp; SEPT 2020] NEUROLOGICAL NURSING</p>
<p>without defective development of the spinal cord, and tends to occur mostly in the lumbar or lumbo sacral region.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>In the milder type (spina bifida oculta), there may be no need for any medical intervention while in the meningocele an meningomyelocele surgical intervention is called for.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pre-and-post-operative-nursing-care">Pre and Post-Operative Nursing Care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pre-and-post-operative-nursing-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The objectives of care should be to prevent infection and injury to the sac, skin damage and urinary tract infection.</li>
<li>These are achieved by performing aseptic technique dressing using warm normal saline until the operation is performed.</li>
<li>The dressing should be changed at least four hourly.</li>
<li>The vital signs should are taken and recorded every two hours and any deviation is reported.</li>
<li>Continuous assessment of childs general condition to include musculo skeletal system is done.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="epilepsy">EPILEPSY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#epilepsy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Epilepsy can be defined as a neurological condition characterised by recurrent seizures.</li>
<li>A seizure is a sudden attack of altered cerebral function.</li>
<li>An epileptic seizure is the result of altered cerebral function caused by abrupt, abnormal and excessive, uncontrolled repetitive electrical discharges of cerebral neurons.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-three-types-of-epilepsy">The Three Types of Epilepsy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-three-types-of-epilepsy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p> Petit Mal (term given to a staring spell; usually less than 15 seconds, begins suddenly and occurs without any warning signs)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Grand Mal</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Jacksonian Epilepsy: Characterised by unilateral chronic (sporadic muscular rigidity and relaxation) movements that start in one group of muscles and then systematically spread to adjacent groups of muscles reflecting the match of epileptic activity through the motor cortex.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Investigations, medical and Nursing management is similar to adults.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Common drugs prescribed may be either/or phenobarbitone (luminal) with a dose of 3-6mg/kg body weight or phenytoin sodium (epanutin), with a dose of 10-20mg/kg body weight.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>NB: An epileptic seizure is a medical emergency! Remember the ABC rule. Ensure a clear Airway, to enable the patient to Breathe and loosen the clothing to facilitate Circulation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="meningococcal-meningitis">MENINGOCOCCAL MENINGITIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#meningococcal-meningitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Meningitis means inflammation of the meninges.</li>
<li>The meninges are membranes that cover and protect the brain and spinal cord.</li>
<li>Causative organisms are Neisseria Meningitis (Meningococc).</li>
<li>This micro-organism is intracellular gram negative diplococcus.</li>
<li>Meningococcal meningitis is an infectious disease that can be passed from one person to another if meningococci are present in the discharges from the nose and mouth.</li>
</ul>
<p>Predisposing factors is similar to those in adults</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Usually the onset is acute and sudden</li>
<li>Older children may complain of a headache that becomes severe and spreads down the neck</li>
<li>The patient becomes pyrexial with tachycardia</li>
<li>Rigors are often present</li>
<li>Pain in the back and limbs</li>
<li>The patients neck and possibly the spinal column become stiff/rigid</li>
<li>Kernigs sign is positive: patient supine with hip flexed to 90; pain and inability to fully extend the knee, Kernigs sign is negative if the patient can fully extend knee</li>
<li>Due to the fever, convulsions may occur</li>
<li>The child cries with a high-pitched voice</li>
<li>Anorexia is usually present</li>
<li>In very young babies, the anterior fontanelle may bulge outwards instead of positive Kernigs sign</li>
<li>The child is irritable, drowsy and goes into a comatose state</li>
<li>Photophobia is usually common and in some cases circulatory collapse with petechial haemorrhage may occur (bleeding spots) on the skin.</li>
<li>Cyanosis and vomiting are present.</li>
</ul>
<p>80</p>
<p>COLLINS &amp; BOSCO [KMTC NRB CAMPUS. MAR &amp; SEPT 2020] NEUROLOGICAL NURSING</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnostic-tests">Diagnostic tests<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-tests" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Begin by taking the patient's personal history.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A physical examination should follow.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A lumbar puncture is performed to analyse the CSF and may show that polymorph cells are increased.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>CSF is turbid in appearance (cloudy), the pressure is raised, glucose level is lower than normal and/or the amount of proteins is raised.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-and-treatment">Nursing Care and Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-and-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The patient is admitted into an isolated cubicle to protect other children</li>
<li>Barrier nursing is instituted for at least the first 48 hours</li>
<li>The room should be quiet and darkened</li>
<li>Shock if present or anticipated, should be effectively managed</li>
<li>Drug therapy should be commenced at once</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="drug-therapy">Drug Therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Crystalline penicillin 300mg (500,000iu)/kg/day, ten times the normal dose given intravenously or intramuscularly three to four hourly until temperature falls, then six hourly for fourteen days.</li>
<li>Chloramphenicol (chloromycetin) can also be administered at 100mg/kg/day IM six hourly until a pyrexial and general condition improves usually five to seven days then change to oral syrup for a total of fourteen days.</li>
<li>Phenobarbitone 5mg/kg/day tds is advised for convulsions up to 10mg tds.</li>
<li>An ampicillin injection may be given in combination with the chloramphenicol and crystapen.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nb">NB/:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nb" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Nuchal rigidity (stiff neck) is an early sign. Any attempts at flexion of the head are difficult because of spasms in the muscles of the neck. Forceful flexion causes severe pain.</li>
<li>Positive Kernig's sign: When the patient is lying with the thigh flexed on the abdomen, the leg cannot be completely extended.</li>
<li>Positive Brudzinski's sign: When the patient's neck is flexed, flexion of the knees and hips is produced; when passive flexion of the lower extremity of one side is made, a similar movement is seen in the opposite extremity.</li>
<li>Photophobia: extreme sensitivity to light; this finding is common, although the cause is unclear</li>
</ul></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div data-testid="stAppIframeResizerAnchor" data-iframe-height="true" class="st-emotion-cache-1dumvfu eht7o1d9"></div></section></div></div></div><div data-testid="portal" id="portal" class="st-emotion-cache-1q6lfs0 e19n7mk11"></div></div><div class=""></div></div>
  

</body></html>

        // Theme toggle functionality
        const themeToggle = document.getElementById('theme-toggle');
        const html = document.documentElement;
        
        themeToggle.addEventListener('click', () => {
            const currentTheme = html.getAttribute('data-theme');
            const newTheme = currentTheme === 'light' ? 'dark' : 'light';
            
            html.setAttribute('data-theme', newTheme);
            localStorage.setItem('theme', newTheme);
        });
        
        // Load saved theme
        const savedTheme = localStorage.getItem('theme') || 'light';
        html.setAttribute('data-theme', savedTheme);
    </script>

# PDF to HTML Conversion System Prompt (v9.4.4) - Rich UI Edition

**Version:** 9.4.4  
**Last Updated:** December 25, 2025  
**Focus:** Modern UI/UX patterns with 100% content fidelity, nested lists, mathematical equations, and comprehensive interactive quiz system

---

## Overview

This is the comprehensive **PDF to HTML Conversion System Prompt - Rich UI Edition**, featuring enhanced content organization patterns, advanced UI components, mathematical equations support, interactive quiz system, and modern design systems while maintaining absolute content fidelity.

## Core Mission

Convert PDF documents into **visually stunning, accessible, and pedagogically effective** HTML pages while ensuring **100% VERBATIM content preservation**. Create highly appealing and effective learning materials with **modern UI/UX patterns**, organized into **logically coherent chunks**, that maintain absolute fidelity to the original text content with interactive quizzes to reinforce learning and assess comprehension.

---

## Image Handling & Lightbox

All images must be wrapped in a `content-figure` container with the `data-lightbox="true"` attribute to enable the click-to-zoom functionality.

### Image Source Reference

**IMPORTANT**: Use the **exact image filenames** as they appear in `content_cleaned.txt`. Do NOT rename or map images.

#### Image Usage Instructions
1. **Check `content_cleaned.txt`** for image references like:
   ```html
   <img src="assets/images/image-20251225-9d805e34.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg">
   ```
2. **Path Resolution Rule**: Use the correct relative path based on the HTML file's location:
   - **Files in `topics/` directory**: Use `../assets/images/`
   - **Files in root directory** (e.g., `index.html`, `comprehensive-exam.html`): Use `assets/images/`
3. **Do NOT rename** images from their timestamp format
4. **Do NOT use** numbered formats like `img-1.jpeg` - use the actual filename

### HTML Structure for Images

```html
<div class="content-figure" data-lightbox="true">
    <div class="figure-image-wrapper">
        <img src="../assets/images/image-20251225-9d805e34.jpeg" alt="[Alt Text]" class="figure-image">
        <div class="figure-overlay">
            <span class="overlay-icon"></span>
            <span class="overlay-text">Click to zoom</span>
        </div>
    </div>
    <p class="figure-caption">Fig. [X.Y]: [Caption Text]</p>
</div>
```

### Image Path Examples

```html
<!-- Correct: Use exact filenames from content_cleaned.txt -->
<img src="../assets/images/image-20251225-9d805e34.jpeg" alt="Gingivitis showing inflamed gums">
<img src="../assets/images/image-20251225-b2c235cf.jpeg" alt="Fibre-optic Endoscope">
<img src="../assets/images/image-20251225-f38697c2.jpeg" alt="Periodontitis diagram">

<!-- Incorrect: Don't use simplified numbered format -->
<img src="../assets/images/img-1.jpeg" alt="...">
<img src="../assets/images/img-12.jpeg" alt="...">
```

---

## Interactive Quiz System

### Quiz System Overview

The quiz system provides 8 different question types to assess learner comprehension. Quizzes are stored in JSON format with versioning support, rendered dynamically via JavaScript, and fully integrated with the existing Rich UI design system.

### Quiz Question Types

#### 1. Multiple Choice (Single Answer)
Standard single-answer questions with 2-6 options.
- **Use Case**: Testing recall of specific facts, definitions, concepts
- **Features**: Radio button selection, immediate feedback, explanation display

#### 2. Multiple Select (Multiple Correct Answers)
Questions where learners select all correct answers.
- **Use Case**: Testing comprehensive understanding of related concepts
- **Features**: Checkbox selection, partial credit option, "Select all that apply" indicator

#### 3. True/False
Binary choice questions for quick knowledge checks.
- **Use Case**: Verifying understanding of statements, common misconceptions
- **Features**: Two-option format, confidence indicator option

#### 4. Fill in the Blank
Text input questions with exact or fuzzy matching.
- **Use Case**: Testing terminology, formulas, key terms
- **Features**: Case-insensitive matching, multiple acceptable answers, hint system
- **CRITICAL**: Question text MUST include `__id__` placeholders (e.g., `__b1__`, `__b2__`) where input fields should appear
- **Example**: `"The liver converts ammonia into __b1__."` with blank ID `"b1"`

#### 5. Matching
Pair items from two columns (drag-and-drop or dropdown).
- **Use Case**: Testing relationships, associations, categorization
- **Features**: Drag-and-drop interface, dropdown fallback, visual feedback

#### 6. Ordering/Sequencing
Arrange items in correct order.
- **Use Case**: Testing processes, procedures, chronological events
- **Features**: Drag-and-drop reordering with live sorting, numbered positions, step validation
- **Implementation Note**: Use "live" sorting during `dragover` events for robust behavior across all environments (including local `file://` protocol).

#### 7. Short Answer
Free-text response with keyword matching.
- **Use Case**: Testing deeper understanding, explanations
- **Features**: Keyword detection, partial credit, model answer display

#### 8. Image-Based Questions
Questions involving image interaction (hotspots, labeling).
- **Use Case**: Anatomy, diagrams, visual identification
- **Features**: Clickable regions, label placement, image zoom

### Media Support (Optional)

Every question can optionally include media (image, video, audio, YouTube) and answer options can optionally include images. All media fields are **optional** - questions work perfectly with text only.

#### Supported Media Types
| Type | Description | Use Case |
|------|-------------|----------|
| `image` | Static image file | Diagrams, photos, charts |
| `video` | Video file (mp4, webm) | Demonstrations, procedures |
| `audio` | Audio file (mp3, wav) | Pronunciation, sounds |
| `youtube` | YouTube embed | Educational videos |

#### Image Answer Options
For multiple-choice and multiple-select questions, each option can optionally include an image. This is useful for visual identification questions where learners select from images rather than text.

####  CRITICAL: Quiz Media Path Resolution
Image and media paths in quiz data files MUST be relative to the **HTML file** that will host the quiz.
- If the quiz is hosted in a file within `topics/` (e.g., `topics/topic-01.html`), use `../assets/images/`.
- If the quiz is hosted in a file in the **root** (e.g., `comprehensive-exam.html`), use `assets/images/`.

### Quiz JSON Schema (v1.0)

Store quiz data in `quizzes/` directory with the following structure:

```
project-name/
 quizzes/
    quiz-schema.json          # Schema definition
    topic-01-quiz.json        # Quiz for topic 01
    topic-02-quiz.json        # Quiz for topic 02
    ...
```

#### Complete Quiz JSON Schema

```json
{
  "$schema": "http://json-schema.org/draft-07/schema#",
  "title": "Quiz Schema v1.0",
  "type": "object",
  "required": ["schemaVersion", "quizId", "metadata", "questions"],
  "properties": {
    "schemaVersion": {
      "type": "string",
      "description": "Schema version for compatibility",
      "pattern": "^\\d+\\.\\d+$",
      "example": "1.0"
    },
    "quizId": {
      "type": "string",
      "description": "Unique identifier for the quiz",
      "pattern": "^[a-z0-9-]+$"
    },
    "metadata": {
      "type": "object",
      "required": ["title", "topicId", "createdAt"],
      "properties": {
        "title": { "type": "string" },
        "description": { "type": "string" },
        "topicId": { "type": "string" },
        "difficulty": { "enum": ["beginner", "intermediate", "advanced"] },
        "estimatedTime": { "type": "integer", "description": "Minutes" },
        "passingScore": { "type": "integer", "minimum": 0, "maximum": 100 },
        "createdAt": { "type": "string", "format": "date-time" },
        "updatedAt": { "type": "string", "format": "date-time" },
        "tags": { "type": "array", "items": { "type": "string" } }
      }
    },
    "settings": {
      "type": "object",
      "properties": {
        "shuffleQuestions": { "type": "boolean", "default": false },
        "shuffleOptions": { "type": "boolean", "default": false },
        "showFeedback": { "enum": ["immediate", "end", "never"], "default": "immediate" },
        "allowRetry": { "type": "boolean", "default": true },
        "showCorrectAnswers": { "type": "boolean", "default": true },
        "timeLimit": { "type": "integer", "description": "Seconds, 0 for unlimited" }
      }
    },
    "questions": {
      "type": "array",
      "items": { "$ref": "#/definitions/question" }
    }
  }
}
```

#### Question Type Definitions

```json
{
  "definitions": {
    "question": {
      "type": "object",
      "required": ["id", "type", "question", "points"],
      "properties": {
        "id": { "type": "string" },
        "type": {
          "enum": [
            "multiple-choice",
            "multiple-select",
            "true-false",
            "fill-blank",
            "matching",
            "ordering",
            "short-answer",
            "image-based"
          ]
        },
        "question": { "type": "string" },
        "points": { "type": "integer", "minimum": 1 },
        "hint": { "type": "string", "description": "OPTIONAL: Hint for the question" },
        "explanation": { "type": "string", "description": "OPTIONAL: Explanation shown after answering" },
        "media": {
          "type": "object",
          "description": "OPTIONAL: Media attachment for the question",
          "properties": {
            "type": { "enum": ["image", "video", "audio", "youtube"] },
            "url": { "type": "string", "description": "URL to media file" },
            "alt": { "type": "string", "description": "Alt text for accessibility" },
            "caption": { "type": "string", "description": "OPTIONAL: Caption below media" },
            "mimeType": { "type": "string", "description": "OPTIONAL: MIME type for video/audio" },
            "videoId": { "type": "string", "description": "YouTube video ID (for youtube type)" },
            "startTime": { "type": "integer", "description": "OPTIONAL: Start time in seconds (youtube)" },
            "autoplay": { "type": "boolean", "default": false },
            "loop": { "type": "boolean", "default": false },
            "muted": { "type": "boolean", "default": false }
          }
        }
      },
      "allOf": [
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "multiple-choice" } } },
          "then": {
            "properties": {
              "options": {
                "type": "array",
                "minItems": 2,
                "maxItems": 6,
                "items": {
                  "type": "object",
                  "required": ["id", "isCorrect"],
                  "properties": {
                    "id": { "type": "string" },
                    "text": { "type": "string", "description": "Text label (OPTIONAL if image provided)" },
                    "isCorrect": { "type": "boolean" },
                    "image": {
                      "type": "object",
                      "description": "OPTIONAL: Image for this option",
                      "properties": {
                        "url": { "type": "string" },
                        "alt": { "type": "string" }
                      }
                    }
                  }
                }
              }
            }
          }
        },
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "multiple-select" } } },
          "then": {
            "properties": {
              "options": {
                "type": "array",
                "items": {
                  "type": "object",
                  "required": ["id", "isCorrect"],
                  "properties": {
                    "id": { "type": "string" },
                    "text": { "type": "string", "description": "Text label (OPTIONAL if image provided)" },
                    "isCorrect": { "type": "boolean" },
                    "image": {
                      "type": "object",
                      "description": "OPTIONAL: Image for this option",
                      "properties": {
                        "url": { "type": "string" },
                        "alt": { "type": "string" }
                      }
                    }
                  }
                }
              },
              "partialCredit": { "type": "boolean", "default": true }
            }
          }
        },
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "true-false" } } },
          "then": {
            "properties": {
              "correctAnswer": { "type": "boolean" }
            }
          }
        },
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "fill-blank" } } },
          "then": {
            "description": " CRITICAL: The 'question' field MUST contain __id__ placeholders (e.g., __b1__, __b2__) that match the blank IDs. Example: 'The liver converts ammonia into __b1__.' with blank id='b1'",
            "properties": {
              "blanks": {
                "type": "array",
                "description": "Array of blank definitions. Each blank.id must have a matching __id__ placeholder in the question text.",
                "items": {
                  "type": "object",
                  "properties": {
                    "id": { "type": "string", "description": "Blank identifier (e.g., 'b1', '1', 'answer1'). Must match placeholder in question." },
                    "acceptedAnswers": { "type": "array", "items": { "type": "string" }, "description": "List of acceptable answers" },
                    "caseSensitive": { "type": "boolean", "default": false }
                  }
                }
              }
            }
          }
        },
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "matching" } } },
          "then": {
            "properties": {
              "pairs": {
                "type": "array",
                "items": {
                  "type": "object",
                  "properties": {
                    "id": { "type": "string" },
                    "left": { "type": "string" },
                    "right": { "type": "string" }
                  }
                }
              }
            }
          }
        },
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "ordering" } } },
          "then": {
            "properties": {
              "items": {
                "type": "array",
                "items": {
                  "type": "object",
                  "properties": {
                    "id": { "type": "string" },
                    "text": { "type": "string" },
                    "correctPosition": { "type": "integer" }
                  }
                }
              }
            }
          }
        },
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "short-answer" } } },
          "then": {
            "properties": {
              "keywords": { "type": "array", "items": { "type": "string" } },
              "minKeywords": { "type": "integer" },
              "modelAnswer": { "type": "string" },
              "maxLength": { "type": "integer" }
            }
          }
        },
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "image-based" } } },
          "then": {
            "properties": {
              "imageUrl": { "type": "string" },
              "imageAlt": { "type": "string" },
              "hotspots": {
                "type": "array",
                "items": {
                  "type": "object",
                  "properties": {
                    "id": { "type": "string" },
                    "x": { "type": "number" },
                    "y": { "type": "number" },
                    "radius": { "type": "number" },
                    "label": { "type": "string" },
                    "isCorrect": { "type": "boolean" }
                  }
                }
              },
              "options": {
                "type": "array",
                "description": "OPTIONAL: Alternative to hotspots for multiple-choice style image questions",
                "items": {
                  "type": "object",
                  "required": ["id", "isCorrect"],
                  "properties": {
                    "id": { "type": "string" },
                    "text": { "type": "string" },
                    "isCorrect": { "type": "boolean" }
                  }
                }
              }
            }
          }
        }
      ]
    }
  }
}
```

```json
{
```

#### Example 5: Fill-Blank Question - Correct vs Incorrect Usage

** CRITICAL REQUIREMENT**: The question text MUST include `__id__` placeholders that match the blank IDs.

#####  CORRECT - Single Blank

```json
{
  "id": "q1",
  "type": "fill-blank",
  "question": "The accumulation of serous fluid in the peritoneal cavity seen in cirrhosis is called __b1__.",
  "points": 10,
  "blanks": [
    { "id": "b1", "acceptedAnswers": ["ascites"], "caseSensitive": false }
  ],
  "explanation": "Ascites is the accumulation of fluid in the peritoneal cavity."
}
```

#####  CORRECT - Multiple Blanks

```json
{
  "id": "q2",
  "type": "fill-blank",
  "question": "The liver converts ammonia into __b1__, which is then excreted by the __b2__.",
  "points": 15,
  "blanks": [
    { "id": "b1", "acceptedAnswers": ["urea"], "caseSensitive": false },
    { "id": "b2", "acceptedAnswers": ["kidneys", "kidney"], "caseSensitive": false }
  ],
  "explanation": "Ammonia is converted to urea by the liver and excreted by the kidneys."
}
```

#####  CORRECT - Numeric IDs

```json
{
  "id": "q3",
  "type": "fill-blank",
  "question": "The heart has __1__ chambers: two __2__ and two __3__.",
  "points": 15,
  "blanks": [
    { "id": "1", "acceptedAnswers": ["four", "4"], "caseSensitive": false },
    { "id": "2", "acceptedAnswers": ["atria", "atriums"], "caseSensitive": false },
    { "id": "3", "acceptedAnswers": ["ventricles"], "caseSensitive": false }
  ]
}
```

#####  INCORRECT - Missing Placeholder

```json
{
  "id": "q_wrong",
  "type": "fill-blank",
  "question": "The accumulation of serous fluid in the peritoneal cavity is called _______.",
  "points": 10,
  "blanks": [
    { "id": "b1", "acceptedAnswers": ["ascites"], "caseSensitive": false }
  ]
}
```
**Problem**: Uses `_______` instead of `__b1__`. The quiz engine won't render an input field!

#####  INCORRECT - Mismatched IDs

```json
{
  "id": "q_wrong2",
  "type": "fill-blank",
  "question": "The liver converts ammonia into __answer__.",
  "points": 10,
  "blanks": [
    { "id": "b1", "acceptedAnswers": ["urea"], "caseSensitive": false }
  ]
}
```
**Problem**: Question uses `__answer__` but blank ID is `b1`. They must match exactly!

##### Key Rules for Fill-Blank Questions:
1. **Placeholder Format**: Use double underscores: `__id__` (not single `_id_` or dashes `---`)
2. **ID Matching**: Placeholder `__b1__` must match blank `"id": "b1"` exactly
3. **Multiple Blanks**: Each blank needs its own unique ID and placeholder
4. **Accepted Answers**: Provide multiple acceptable variations (e.g., `["urea", "Urea"]`)
5. **Case Sensitivity**: Set `caseSensitive: false` for most medical terminology



### Quiz Loading Methods

The quiz system supports 3 loading methods (tried in order):

| Method | Attribute | Works with file:// | Requires Server |
|--------|-----------|-------------------|-----------------|
| **JSONP (Recommended)** | `data-quiz-js` |  Yes | No |
| Fetch API | `data-quiz-src` |  No | Yes |
| Embedded JSON | `<script id="quiz-data-[id]">` |  Yes | No |

#### Method 1: JSONP Script Loading (Recommended)

**Best for:** Opening HTML files directly in browser (`file://` protocol)

Create quiz as a `.js` file that calls `registerQuiz()`:

```javascript
// quizzes/topic-01-quiz.js
registerQuiz("topic-01-quiz", {
  "schemaVersion": "1.0",
  "quizId": "topic-01-quiz",
  "metadata": { ... },
  "questions": [ ... ]
});
```

HTML usage:
```html
<div class="quiz-container" 
     data-quiz-id="topic-01-quiz"
     data-quiz-js="../quizzes/topic-01-quiz.js">
```

#### Method 2: Fetch API (Requires Web Server)

**Best for:** Deployment on web servers (http/https)

```html
<div class="quiz-container" 
     data-quiz-id="topic-01-quiz"
     data-quiz-src="../quizzes/topic-01-quiz.json">
```

#### Method 3: Embedded JSON

**Best for:** Single-file distribution

```html
<script type="application/json" id="quiz-data-topic-01-quiz">
{
  "schemaVersion": "1.0",
  "quizId": "topic-01-quiz",
  ...
}
</script>

<div class="quiz-container" data-quiz-id="topic-01-quiz">
```

### Quiz HTML Integration

Add quiz sections to topic pages using this structure:

```html
<!-- Quiz Section -->
<section class="quiz-section" id="topic-quiz" aria-labelledby="quiz-title">
    <div class="quiz-header">
        <div class="quiz-badge">
            <span class="quiz-icon"></span>
            <span>Knowledge Check</span>
        </div>
        <h2 id="quiz-title" class="quiz-title">Test Your Understanding</h2>
        <p class="quiz-description">Complete this quiz to assess your comprehension of the topic.</p>
    </div>
    
    <!-- Quiz Container - JSONP method (works with file://) -->
    <div class="quiz-container" 
         data-quiz-id="topic-01-quiz"
         data-quiz-js="../quizzes/topic-01-quiz.js">
        
        <!-- Loading State -->
        <div class="quiz-loading">
            <div class="quiz-spinner"></div>
            <p>Loading quiz...</p>
        </div>
        
        <!-- Quiz Content (injected by JS) -->
        <div class="quiz-content" hidden></div>
        
        <!-- Quiz Results (shown after completion) -->
        <div class="quiz-results" hidden></div>
    </div>
</section>
```
